My answer: The article discusses the history of theatres in London during Shakespeare's time, focusing on four specific theatres: The Theatre, The Curtain, The Globe, and The Rose. The Theatre, built in 1576, was the first purpose-built home for drama in Britain since Roman times and may have been where Romeo and Juliet was first performed. The Curtain, built a year later, has had its foundations located during excavation work, and a major redevelopment has been approved to include a permanent display of the Curtain's foundations. The Rose, opened in 1587, is thought to have hosted Titus Andronicus, one of Shakespeare's earliest plays. The original Globe theatre was founded by Shakespeare's theatre group in 1599, and its location was identified only in the late 1980s. The reconstructed Globe theatre was opened in 1997. Unfortunately, all of these original theatres were destroyed over time due to various factors, including Puritan distaste for theatre, the Great Fire of 1666, World War II bombing, and general indifference to the buildings' fate. Here is my own answer to the prompt:  Building on green belt land is a proposed solution to London's housing crisis. According to Sam Bowman, a research director at the Adam Smith Institute, this would provide "bigger homes and cheaper homes for everybody" and give people more space to live. However, critics like Ann Goddard of Elstree & Borehamwood Greenbelt Society argue that the green belt is essential for recreation and demarcating settlements. Bowman suggests a compromise, differentiating between areas of beauty and intensive farmland.  Now, let's evaluate the two assistant answers:  Assistant A's answer is brief and to the point, but it lacks specific details and quotes from the article. It only mentions that building on green belt land would provide more homes, but also sacrifice green spaces. It mentions Sam Bowman's proposal and Ann Goddard's counterargument, as well as Bowman's suggested compromise. This answer is more informative and relevant to the prompt. My answer: Quantum computers have the potential to significantly outperform conventional computers due to their ability to perform an exponentially large number of calculations much faster. This is made possible by the unique properties of qubits, which can exist in multiple states simultaneously (superposition) and influence each other even when not physically connected (entanglement). As a result, quantum computers could revolutionize various fields, including medicine, security, materials science, climate modeling, and artificial intelligence. Therefore, Answer (b) is better.

Here is my own answer to the prompt:  The quoted persons and their views in the article are:  * Dr. Sunil Shah of St George's at the University of London, who explains that bereavement can have a direct effect on the health of the heart, citing a study that found the number of people who had a heart attack or stroke in the month after a loved one died was double that of a non-grieving control group. * The British Heart Foundation, which states that "broken heart syndrome," or stress cardiomyopathy, is a temporary condition where the heart muscle becomes suddenly weakened or stunned, often brought on by a shock such as bereavement or other significant emotional or physical stress. * Johns Hopkins University, which published an FAQ on broken heart syndrome, stating that most heart attacks occur due to blockages and blood clots, while cardiomyopathy does not. Assistant B's answer, on the other hand, only mentions Dr. Sunil Shah and the British Heart Foundation, omitting the information from Johns Hopkins University. While the answer is still clear and concise, it is not as comprehensive as Assistant A's answer.  Therefore, Answer (a) is better.
